\doxysubsection{Description détaillée}
Libsodium compatibility layer

This is the only class you should be interfacing with, as a user of sodium\+\_\+compat.

If the PHP extension for libsodium is installed, it will always use that instead of our implementations. You get better performance and stronger guarantees against side-\/channels that way.

However, if your users don\textquotesingle{}t have the PHP extension installed, we offer a compatible interface here. It will give you the correct results as if the PHP extension was installed. It won\textquotesingle{}t be as fast, of course.

CAUTION \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} CAUTION \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} CAUTION \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} CAUTION \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} CAUTION \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} CAUTION \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} CAUTION \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} CAUTION \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item Until audited, this is probably not safe to use! DANGER WILL ROBINSON \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}
\item CAUTION \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} CAUTION \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} CAUTION \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} CAUTION \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} CAUTION \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} CAUTION \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} CAUTION \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} CAUTION \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} 
\end{DoxyItemize}

Authenticated Encryption with Associated Data\+: Decryption

Algorithm\+: Cha\+Cha20-\/\+Poly1305

This mode uses a 64-\/bit random nonce with a 64-\/bit counter. IETF mode uses a 96-\/bit random nonce with a 32-\/bit counter.


\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Paramètres}
string & {\em \$ciphertext} & Encrypted message (with Poly1305 MAC appended) \\
\hline
string & {\em \$assoc\+Data} & Authenticated Associated Data (unencrypted) \\
\hline
string & {\em \$nonce} & Number to be used only Once; must be 8 bytes \\
\hline
string & {\em \$key} & Encryption key\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Renvoie}
string The original plaintext message

{\footnotesize\ttfamily static crypto\+\_\+auth (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{\$message,  }\item[{}]{\$key }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [static]}}

Authenticate a message. Uses symmetric-\/key cryptography.

Algorithm\+: HMAC-\/\+SHA512-\/256. Which is HMAC-\/\+SHA-\/512 truncated to 256 bits. Not to be confused with HMAC-\/\+SHA-\/512/256 which would use the SHA-\/512/256 hash function (uses different initial parameters but still truncates to 256 bits to sidestep length-\/extension attacks).


\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Paramètres}
string & {\em \$message} & Message to be authenticated \\
\hline
string & {\em \$key} & Symmetric authentication key \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Renvoie}
string Message authentication code 
\end{DoxyReturn}

\begin{DoxyExceptions}{Exceptions}
{\em Sodium\+Exception} & \\
\hline
{\em Type\+Error} & @psalm-\/suppress Mixed\+Argument \\
\hline
\end{DoxyExceptions}

\Hypertarget{class_paragon_i_e___sodium___compat_a365b1e0c8a6ae743433064cd65b539d8}\label{class_paragon_i_e___sodium___compat_a365b1e0c8a6ae743433064cd65b539d8} 
\index{ParagonIE\_Sodium\_Compat@{ParagonIE\_Sodium\_Compat}!crypto\_box@{crypto\_box}}
\index{crypto\_box@{crypto\_box}!ParagonIE\_Sodium\_Compat@{ParagonIE\_Sodium\_Compat}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{crypto\_box()}{crypto\_box()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily static crypto\+\_\+box (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{\$plaintext,  }\item[{}]{\$nonce,  }\item[{}]{\$keypair }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [static]}}

Authenticated asymmetric-\/key encryption. Both the sender and recipient may decrypt messages.

Algorithm\+: X25519-\/\+XSalsa20-\/\+Poly1305. X25519\+: Elliptic-\/\+Curve Diffie Hellman over Curve25519. XSalsa20\+: Extended-\/nonce variant of salsa20. Poyl1305\+: Polynomial MAC for one-\/time message authentication.


\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Paramètres}
string & {\em \$plaintext} & The message to be encrypted \\
\hline
string & {\em \$nonce} & A Number to only be used Once; must be 24 bytes \\
\hline
string & {\em \$keypair} & Your secret key and your recipient\textquotesingle{}s public key \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Renvoie}
string Ciphertext with 16-\/byte Poly1305 MAC 
\end{DoxyReturn}

\begin{DoxyExceptions}{Exceptions}
{\em Sodium\+Exception} & \\
\hline
{\em Type\+Error} & @psalm-\/suppress Mixed\+Argument \\
\hline
\end{DoxyExceptions}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily static crypto\+\_\+box\+\_\+keypair (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}{ }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [static]}}

Generate a new random X25519 keypair.

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Renvoie}
string A 64-\/byte string; the first 32 are your secret key, while the last 32 are your public key. crypto\+\_\+box\+\_\+secretkey() and crypto\+\_\+box\+\_\+publickey() exist to separate them so you don\textquotesingle{}t accidentally get them mixed up! 
\end{DoxyReturn}

\index{ParagonIE\_Sodium\_Compat@{ParagonIE\_Sodium\_Compat}!crypto\_box\_seal@{crypto\_box\_seal}}
\index{crypto\_box\_seal@{crypto\_box\_seal}!ParagonIE\_Sodium\_Compat@{ParagonIE\_Sodium\_Compat}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{crypto\_box\_seal()}{crypto\_box\_seal()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily static crypto\+\_\+box\+\_\+seal (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{\$plaintext,  }\item[{}]{\$public\+Key }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [static]}}

Anonymous public-\/key encryption. Only the recipient may decrypt messages.

Algorithm\+: X25519-\/\+XSalsa20-\/\+Poly1305, as with crypto\+\_\+box. The sender\textquotesingle{}s X25519 keypair is ephemeral. Nonce is generated from the BLAKE2b hash of both public keys.

This provides ciphertext integrity.


\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Paramètres}
string & {\em \$plaintext} & Message to be sealed \\
\hline
string & {\em \$public\+Key} & Your recipient\textquotesingle{}s public key \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Renvoie}
string Sealed message that only your recipient can decrypt 
\end{DoxyReturn}

\begin{DoxyExceptions}{Exceptions}
{\em Sodium\+Exception} & \\
\hline
{\em Type\+Error} & @psalm-\/suppress Mixed\+Argument \\
\hline
\end{DoxyExceptions}

Opens a message encrypted with crypto\+\_\+box\+\_\+seal(). Requires the recipient\textquotesingle{}s keypair (sk \texorpdfstring{$\vert$}{|}\texorpdfstring{$\vert$}{|} pk) to decrypt successfully.

This validates ciphertext integrity.

\Hypertarget{class_paragon_i_e___sodium___compat_af9721ad6353f0f22efbf3089d28e5b75}\label{class_paragon_i_e___sodium___compat_af9721ad6353f0f22efbf3089d28e5b75} 
\index{ParagonIE\_Sodium\_Compat@{ParagonIE\_Sodium\_Compat}!crypto\_kx@{crypto\_kx}}
\index{crypto\_kx@{crypto\_kx}!ParagonIE\_Sodium\_Compat@{ParagonIE\_Sodium\_Compat}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{crypto\_kx()}{crypto\_kx()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily static crypto\+\_\+kx (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{\$my\+\_\+secret,  }\item[{}]{\$their\+\_\+public,  }\item[{}]{\$client\+\_\+public,  }\item[{}]{\$server\+\_\+public,  }\item[{}]{\$dont\+Fallback = {\ttfamily false} }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [static]}}

Perform a key exchange, between a designated client and a server.

Typically, you would designate one machine to be the client and the other to be the server. The first two keys are what you\textquotesingle{}d expect for scalarmult() below, but the latter two public keys don\textquotesingle{}t swap places.

\texorpdfstring{$\vert$}{|} ALICE \texorpdfstring{$\vert$}{|} BOB \texorpdfstring{$\vert$}{|} \tabulinesep=1mm
\begin{longtabu}spread 0pt [c]{*{2}{|X[-1]}|}
\hline
\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ Client   }&\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ Server    }\\\cline{1-2}
\endfirsthead
\hline
\endfoot
\hline
\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ Client   }&\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ Server    }\\\cline{1-2}
\endhead
shared = crypto\+\_\+kx(   &shared = crypto\+\_\+kx(   \\\cline{1-2}
\end{longtabu}
\texorpdfstring{$\vert$}{|} alice\+\_\+sk, \texorpdfstring{$\vert$}{|} bob\+\_\+sk, \texorpdfstring{$\vert$}{|} \texorpdfstring{$<$}{<}-\/ contextual \texorpdfstring{$\vert$}{|} bob\+\_\+pk, \texorpdfstring{$\vert$}{|} alice\+\_\+pk, \texorpdfstring{$\vert$}{|} \texorpdfstring{$<$}{<}-\/ contextual \texorpdfstring{$\vert$}{|} alice\+\_\+pk, \texorpdfstring{$\vert$}{|} alice\+\_\+pk, \texorpdfstring{$\vert$}{|} \texorpdfstring{$<$}{<}-\/-\/--- static \texorpdfstring{$\vert$}{|} bob\+\_\+pk \texorpdfstring{$\vert$}{|} bob\+\_\+pk \texorpdfstring{$\vert$}{|} \texorpdfstring{$<$}{<}-\/-\/--- static \texorpdfstring{$\vert$}{|} ) \texorpdfstring{$\vert$}{|} ) \texorpdfstring{$\vert$}{|}

They are used along with the scalarmult product to generate a 256-\/bit BLAKE2b hash unique to the client and server keys.


\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Paramètres}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{use\_fallback()}{use\_fallback()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily static use\+\_\+fallback (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{\$sodium\+\_\+func\+\_\+name = {\ttfamily \textquotesingle{}\textquotesingle{}} }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [static]}, {\ttfamily [protected]}}

Should we use the libsodium core function instead? This is always a good idea, if it\textquotesingle{}s available. (Unless we\textquotesingle{}re in the middle of running our unit test suite.)

If ext/libsodium is available, use it. Return TRUE. Otherwise, we have to use the code provided herein. Return FALSE.
